text:
This is an awesome an super quick recipe.  I am very picky about my slaw and prefer the slaw from Long John Silver's Restuarant.  This slaw taste just like their slaw, sweet and tangy.  I used pre-shredded cabbage and carrots, light mayo and splenda sugar. I also added a bit a black pepper because I like pepper in my slaw.  It was perfect after just putting it together and I am sure it will be even better tomorrow. THANKS!!!

This is a great homestyle coleslaw. Very creamy, mild flavor. This had a smooth mellow sweet taste. I only let it sit about thirty minutes before we ate it. I'll bet it'll be even better tomorrow. DH and I both liked this one. Great for picky eaters as there is no onion or green pepper. All I added was about 1/2 tsp kosher salt and 1/4 tsp ground black pepper. This was really fast and easy, a great recipe! Thanks Denise, this is a keeper.

text:
I was looking for an easy & quick prep recipe since I had some left over cabbage set aside. I guess I didn't pay close enough attention to the part about this family favorite being from a Pennsylvania cook! This slaw tastes nothing like most southern coleslaw recipes that I'm more familiar with, but I was actually quite pleased with the flavor! My husband said it tastes like the KFC recipe and that's the only commercial slaw I prefer!    I loved the sweet/tangy flavor and gave it a 4 because I think its worth making a few times to figure out if yours is too soupy or watery the way others describe...I'm so used to the mayo-filled southern style salad, that the soupiness caught me a little by surprise.  I will make again though!

text:
Yes, to add to everyone else, this IS the most delicious coleslaw recipe!  At first, it just seemed too simple to be good, but I read the other reviews and was convinced!  I have made this about 5 times.  The first three were as is.  I do agree, however, with others that the sugar is too much for my liking, so I do reduce that by about half.  Also, using white vinegar still produces a wonderful salad, but DO make it with the apple cider vinegar again when you have a chance because the subtle difference in flavor REALLY makes a difference to send this one over the edge!  Another wonderful variation is to use half green cabbage and half purple/red cabbage.  I love the colors of the red, white, and orange.  Very pretty, and the red cabbage has extra vitamins that are very wonderful!

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
My sister-in-law went crazy over this coleslaw when I made it once and has tried to duplicate it many times. She follows the same recipe, but insists that mine is always better. I finally figured out that the reason her slaw isn't as flavorful is because she uses the prepackaged cabbage/carrot mix from the store, whereas I actually take the time to shred it all fresh. By the time I'm done making mine, the "sauce" is actually tinted orange from the juice of my finely shredded carrots. Hers is always pure white. I also believe that freshly cut cabbage is far more moist and flavorful than the packaged stuff. 

I admit that I had to read an online tutorial about how to properly shred cabbage (Google search: "Five Reasons to Shred Cabbage with a Knife, and How To Do It" to find the article I read) but it turned out to be quite easy and I've done it many times since. I've HAD to since everyone in the family keeps demanding I make it! I also like things extra tangy so I usually up the ACV to 1/3 cup, though I'm not positive it makes a noticeable difference.

city:

country:

text:
Great coleslaw! I have been trying to perfect my recipe and for some reason the proportions were always off..too sweet, too sour..too many extra unneeded veggies. This is really the best coleslaw recipe because it's so simple and easy! I shredded my own cabbage since the pre-shredded bag in the grocery store was so overpriced I couldn't bring myself to buy it. I also used organic carrots which are way sweeter than the conventional kind. Try them! You'll want to eat carrots every day! Also, be sure to use Bragg's raw, unfiltered apple cider vinegar. It has a wonderful cloudy appearance and the flavor is amazing. It takes salad dressings to a whole new level. Not like the other brands which are so processed, sharp and acidic. Also added some fresh ground pepper for a little bite. Wonderful recipe, thanks for sharing!

I love this recipe because it really, truly is as easy as it seems. No additional seasonings needed. Super flavorful, right balance of creamy with sour. Only comment is that I used a 10 oz bag of shredded cabbage to start and there was way too much dressing. Very soupy once the coleslaw wilted down. I doubled the vinegar and sugar and brought it to a boil together then added about a teaspoon of dry mustard, 1 teaspoon of salt and half a teaspoon fresh, finely ground black pepper....mixed it well to dissolve the sugar then dressed the cabbage mix to which I added a quarter of a Spanish onion shredded. I added 3/4 cup of mayonnaise. Absolutely the best coleslaw I've ever made. I like mine quite wet so that's why I added the extra ratio of vinegar/sugar.

this was my first time making cole slaw and it was easy to make and yummy!  i added a half cup of raisins and some pepper as well.  also....when i made it, it didn't seem like i had enough dressing (i prefer mine a bit more liquidy), so i added a tiny bit more mayo, sugar and vinegar.  mistake!  i didn't realize that it would take a bit for it to get a bit more liquidy as it sat.  next time, i'll let it sit longer.  

anyway.  yummy!  i will totally make this again.  : )
